## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator, which in mechanics is determined by a restoring force derived from a potential (often a nonlinear function of position x) and may also include explicit time-dependent driving or parametric excitation via t. With only x and t available, common models express dv_dt as a nonlinear function of x plus optional periodic/slowly varying forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke (linear oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring force)
- Biased equilibrium (constant load/offset): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (gravity offset, DC forcing, shifted equilibrium)
- Quadratic nonlinearity (asymmetric spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (broken symmetry in restoring force)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (strong nonlinearity at large amplitude)
- Pendulum restoring law: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (rotational oscillator; small-angle limit gives linear in x)
- Saturating/softening restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) (bounded force at large |x|)
- Double-well potential (symmetry-breaking): dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (bistable oscillator; wells for suitable signs)
- Polynomial potential with bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 + c2 (tilted Duffing / constant forcing)
- Harmonic driving (forced oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3) (external periodic forcing)
- Multi-tone/complex forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (superposed periodic drives)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x (Mathieu-type structure)
- Nonlinear parametric stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (parametrically excited Duffing)
- Impact/stop-like piecewise stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Max(x - c2, 0) (unilateral contact or end-stop behavior)
- Singular/strong repulsive core (effective constraint): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 / (x**2 + c2) (repulsion near x=0; regularized singular force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative autonomous oscillator (no explicit forcing) → dv_dt depends on x only; time t should not appear if energy is conserved and parameters are constant.
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt is typically an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x^3, -sin(c*x)); even-power terms (x**2, x**4) indicate asymmetry/bias.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive cubic contribution to the restoring magnitude (e.g., -c0*x - c1*x**3 with c1>0) suggests hardening; opposite sign suggests softening and potential amplitude-dependent frequency shifts.
- Bistability/double-well dynamics: terms like dv_dt = c0*x - c1*x**3 (or equivalently derived from U(x)= -c0*x**2 + c1*x**4) indicate two stable equilibria separated by an unstable one.
- Angle-like coordinate periodicity: sinusoidal restoring force in x (sin(c*x)) suggests x is an angle (pendulum/rotor) and the force is periodic in x, unlike polynomial springs.
- Bounded restoring force at large displacement: tanh(c*x) or similar sigmoids imply the acceleration saturates for large |x| (finite-force limit, yielding softer response than polynomials).
- External periodic driving: additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms indicate a forced oscillator; resonance phenomena are associated with matching drive frequency to the system’s natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance: multiplicative coupling of x with a periodic function of t, (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicates time-varying stiffness (Mathieu-type), leading to instability tongues in parameter space.
- Contact/impact constraints: piecewise terms like Max(x-c,0) reflect unilateral springs/stops, producing non-smooth acceleration and potentially higher harmonics/chaos even without explicit velocity terms.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):
\[
f(x,t)=0.4226191609\,\sin t\;-\;1.1535719134\,x\;-\;1.1535719134\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
Key structural requirements:
1) A pure time sinusoid term \(A\sin t\) (no \(x\) in it).
2) A linear-in-\(x\) term \(B x\).
3) A *non-polynomial, non-separable* term \(C\,x e^{-|x|}\) involving \(|x|\). This is essential and cannot be replaced by any polynomial/power series exactly on a domain where \(x\) can be negative.

Trigonometric note: any candidate term \(c0\cos(c1+t)\) can match \(0.4226\sin t\) by choosing \(c0=0.4226\) and \(c1=-\pi/2\) (since \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\)). So the time forcing is not the blocker.

Now check candidates for the crucial \(x e^{-|x|}\) structure (or anything that could become it by parameter choice). None of the candidates contain \(\exp(\cdot)\) or \(|x|\). Therefore, the only way they could match GT is if the GT’s \(x e^{-|x|}\) term could be made to disappear—but GT constants are fixed and that coefficient is \(-1.1535\neq 0\). So any candidate lacking an \(x e^{-|x|}\) term cannot be globally equivalent.

Still, I’ll briefly classify each candidate:

1. \(c0\cos(c1+t)+c2\sin(c3x+c4)+c5x^3+c6x^{c7}+c8x+x\). Only trig-in-\(x\) and algebraic powers of \(x\); no \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -1.15357191344644*x - 1.15357191344644*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.422619160916855*sin(t)**

Key observations about the GT:
- It has a `sin(t)` term (equivalently `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift)
- It has a linear term in `x`
- It has a term `x*exp(-|x|)` which is NOT a polynomial, NOT a power law `x^c`, and NOT expressible as `sin(cx)` or any finite polynomial/power combination

The critical question is: **Can `x*exp(-|x|)` be represented by the basis functions in each candidate?**

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is:
- For x > 0: `x*exp(-x)`
- For x < 0: `x*exp(x)`

This is NOT equivalent to any polynomial, power law `x^c`, `sin(cx)`, or combination thereof. Since x takes both positive and negative values, `|x|` matters and `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be written as `x^c` for any constant c.

Let me check if any candidate has the right basis functions:

**Most candidates** contain combinations of: `cos(c+t)`, `x^c`, `x^3`, `x^5`, `sin(cx+c)`, `x`, and various `t`-dependent terms.

None of these basis functions can produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is transcendental in x and cannot be expressed as any finite combination of power laws, polynomials, or trigonometric functions of x.

Let me verify each candidate type:
- `x^c` for any fixed c: This is a power law, not `x*exp(-|x|)`
- `sin(cx+d)`: Trigonometric, linearly independent from exponentials
- `x^3, x^5`: Polynomial terms
- `x/(c+t)^n`: Rational in t, still linear in x
- `x*(c+t)^c`: Power of t times x

**Candidates 36, 37**: Have `c3*x^c4 + c5*x^c6` - two power law terms. Even with two different powers, a sum of power laws cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x (especially since x takes both signs, and `x^c` with non-integer c is problematic for negative x).

**Candidate 38**: Has `sin(c3*t+c4)` plus `x^c6 + x^3 + x`. The extra sin term is in t, not helping with the x-dependence.

No candidate contains `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(x)` or any exponential function of x. Therefore, none can match the GT.
